>     - ‚úÖ **STEP 2 COMPLETE 2026-06-04. $9A0F RESOLVED as a sanctioned honest goto ‚Äî and it's the LONE one.** Census (`single-header ‚â•2-back-edge loops still without a while/do construct`) returns **exactly 1 across all 4 banks: `$99D2`/`$9A0F` `ai_place_combat_units_random_or_smart`** ‚Äî every other step-2-class menu loop is folded. `$9A0F` is genuinely unfoldable *soundly*: it's a FULLY-ROTATED multi-back-edge loop ‚Äî the header `$9A0F` (which also does the per-iteration `commit_unit_move_and_redraw_count(rng,rng)` work) sits at the **highest** address while its real body-entry `$99F9` is laid out **after** the `slot++` continue block `$99EF`. A top-test `while` resolves the body-entry to the listing-first block (`$99EF`) instead of the bytecode entry (`$99F9`) ‚Üí the gate REJECTS it (divergence `struct $9A0F‚Üí$99EF` vs `raw‚Üí$99F9`); fixing it would need body REORDERING, which the $8C88 work proved is unsound under the address-based lowering. `while(1)` doesn't fit either (the header must OPEN the span ‚Äî `_fold_while1` line 1511 ‚Äî but it's at the bottom of the address range). So it correctly reverts to honest goto (one of the 35 fallbacks). This is exactly the EPIC's "leave an honest goto where the bytecode layout is genuinely tangled ‚Äî correct, not a failure." **The whole step-2 menu-loop class is now folded or honestly-goto'd; ‚ñ∂ the remaining loop frontier is STEP 3 (the 6 two-test `both` loops above) + the 68 multi-HEADER nested/sibling subs (the big separate bucket).** [[feedback_transpilation_as_grounding]]
> - üü¢ **Phase 3 ‚Äî `switch` body inlining ‚Äî STEP 1 DONE 2026-06-04. ‚öÝÔ∏è KEY FINDING: "only 3 clean" was a measurement error ‚Äî the real prize is 29/38.** The metric was wrong: C `switch` does fall-through NATIVELY (and this VM's switch is first-class ‚Äî `$D5`/`$D9`), so the test is **single-entry dispatch** (every case target dominated by the switch block ‚Üí the bodies can move INSIDE the braces), NOT "break-separated bodies." By that test **29 of 38 switches are FORMALIZABLE**; only **9 stay goto-cases** (a case body entered from OUTSIDE the switch ‚Äî irreducible; 8 of them are the step-2 `while(1)` menu loops where `continue` re-enters a case). Survey tool `tools/probe-switch-shapes.py`. **Chris's call (option 1): formalize EVERY single-entry switch ‚Äî bodies inside the braces, honest internal `goto` local to the case where fall-through can't reach** (vs only folding pure-break ones). **STEP 1 landed 12 of the 25 the detector finds** (the interleaved-merge ones, which converge via goto and need no `break`): the shared detector `vm_cfg.switch_dispatches` (single-entry test + S-dominated enclosed span; **both** the emit and the gate consume it, so they can't disagree ‚Äî the `value_diamonds` pattern) ‚Üí `vm_decompile.structure_switches` (runs LAST, after loops+if/else, so it never reorders body lines: lexical order == address order is preserved, keeping the address-based gate faithful AND the C correct) drops the `case N: goto L_X` dispatch lines, moves the bodies inside the braces with inline `case N:`/`default:` labels, prunes the now-unreferenced case-target labels ‚Üí `vm_cfg.lower_struct_cfg` reads the switch header's successors from the inline `case` labels (`switch_edges`, parallel to `header_edges`/`dowhile_edges`). **Three real traps caught + handled:** (a) body cut off mid-block (`brace_close` is the last block's LEADER, not its end ‚Üí added `body_end`); (b) the lexical-vs-address gap ‚Äî `structure_lines` folds an `if{}` whose braces cross a `case:` boundary and swallow the next case (`$95BE`, legal-but-ugly Duff's-device C the address gate would accept) ‚Üí a **lexical-foldability guard** (every case target must sit at brace-depth 0) skips those, leaving them honest goto-cases; (c) a switch fold that breaks the gate now PROGRESSIVELY falls back (drop switch ‚Üí drop loop+switch ‚Üí goto) so it never costs a sub its other valid folds. **Reads as source now:** `per_period_fief_daimyo_update_driver` ($A30D) = `switch(current_season){ case 1: highwater reset; case 2: harvest; case 3: relations decay; case 0/default: aging }`. Gates ALL green: cfg-gate 495/495 + 495/495 (**35 fallbacks UNCHANGED ‚Äî zero regression**), round-trip 495/45024 CLEAN, --check 0 BAD √ó4, drift CLEAN, decompiled diff is a pure structural transform (`git diff -w`: +`case`/+`}`/‚àí`goto L_X`/‚àí`L_X:`). **Non-vacuousness PROVEN** ‚Äî `test-vm-cfg.py` 94‚Üí**106**: a dropped case label (lost dispatch edge) is REJECTED (existential ‚Äî a router-shared case is genuinely CFG-neutral, contraction absorbs it; the gate is right to accept that). ‚ñ∂ STEP 2 = the clean-trailing-merge switches (the fall-through ladders). ‚ñ∂ STEP 3 = the nested-case-target switches.
>   - üü¢ **STEP 2 DONE 2026-06-04 ‚Äî the fall-through ladders, +4 (12‚Üí16 of 25). KEY: no `break` keyword needed.** A case targeting the trailing merge M (== `body_end`, the block right AFTER the `}`) is emitted as an **EMPTY trailing case that falls through the `}` to M** ‚Äî fall-off-the-switch IS break semantics, and the address-based gate already models it as a fall to `body_end`, so NO `break;` keyword and NO switch break-context in the gate were needed (simpler than the loop break substrate). One change in `structure_switches`: after the body walk, any case target not placed inside the territory but equal to `body_end` gets an empty `case`/`default:` label before the `}`. **`ai_terrain_strength_term` ($9BB4) now reads as the textbook ladder** ‚Äî `local11 = 3; switch(terrain){ case 32: local11--; case 16: local11--; case 8: local11--; default: } return ‚Ä¶` (`= 3 ‚àí count`). Gates green: cfg-gate 495/495 + 495/495 (**35 fallbacks UNCHANGED**), round-trip CLEAN, --check 0 BAD, drift CLEAN, test-vm-cfg **106** ($9BB4 ladder added as a fixture: folds + a dropped ladder case is REJECTED). ‚ñ∂ STEP 3 = the remaining 9.
>   - üü¢ **STEP 3 DONE 2026-06-04 ‚Äî the fold BARRIER, +2 (16‚Üí18 of 25) AND fallbacks improved 35‚Üí34.** `structure_lines` gained a `case_barriers` param (the switch case-target addresses, computed from `switch_dispatches` before it runs): a braced `if{}`/`if-else` fold whose body `[i+1, fold_end)` would ENCLOSE a case target is suppressed ‚Üí that case target stays at brace-depth 0 so `structure_switches` can inline the switch (the local `if` just keeps its goto). **Freed `$95BE` (the malformed-Duff's-device case from step 1) and `$A2D2` (was a gate-reject ‚Üí now folds cleanly, hence one FEWER fallback than baseline).** Diff is a pure structural transform (`git diff -w` = only `case`/`default:`/`}`/`goto`/`L_`/`switch`/`if (` tokens ‚Äî the barrier reverts a few if-folds to goto, both faithful). Gates green: cfg-gate 495/495 + 495/495 (**34 fallbacks**), round-trip 495/45024 CLEAN, --check 0 BAD √ó4, drift CLEAN, test-vm-cfg 106. **‚ñ∂‚ñ∂ PHASE 3 SUBSTANTIALLY COMPLETE ‚Äî 18 of 25 detected switches inlined (and 9 of 38 total were always honest goto: a case body entered from outside the switch).** The **7 residue** (`$8A4E`,`$8DFD`,`$ADF6`,`$8488` + the `while(1)`-nested `$AB22`,`$AC11`,`$B6B4`) are switches nested INSIDE an outer `if{}`/`while{}` where the switch's territory boundary collides with the OUTER closing braces (addr-0 scaffold the address-based body-walk can't attribute to switch-vs-outer) ‚Äî folding them soundly needs a brace-aware `structure_switches` (track nesting, place the switch `}` relative to outer braces), a real redesign for diminishing returns. They correctly **stay honest goto-cases** ‚Äî the epic's sanctioned "leave a goto where the bytecode/layout is genuinely tangled." [[feedback_transpilation_as_grounding]]
> - **Success = "reads like C, with a few honest gotos where the bytecode genuinely is spaghetti."** Each phase measured by goto-reduction count; each commit gated by CFG-equivalence + the existing round-trip/--check/drift-guard staying green (those still apply ‚Äî bytecode & disasm are untouched; only the C *rendering* changes). [[feedback_transpilation_as_grounding]] [[project_nobunaga_vm_decompiler]]

### EPIC: "See the whole picture" ‚Äî full bytecode‚ÜíC decode, PERSISTED
> The core gap (Chris, 2026-05-29): **the C decompiler output is never stored ‚Äî we regenerate it every session.** It's deterministic (fixed ROM ‚Üí identical C forever), so re-deriving it is pure waste ‚Äî the SRT-cleaning tell on the project's most valuable output. The fix this whole restructure was designed for: **decompile once, commit the `.c`, read it like a codebase.**
> Status verified 2026-05-29: VM-disasm covers only **4 of 16 banks** (00/01/02/15); C decompile is per-subroutine and ephemeral. No persisted whole-bank C exists.
- [x] 1. Recover/rebuild `vm-disasm.py` and save it. **DONE 2026-05-30** ‚Äî `tools/vm-disasm.py`, built on execution-validated `OPCODE_INFO` lengths + handler-decoded `$D5`/`$D9` variable-length switches + recursive-descent reachability termination. Validated by **exact-tiling** (the 135/131/131/98 stubs must tile each bank): **0 misaligned across all 495 subs**.
- [x] 2. Dump banks **03‚Äì14** ‚Üí reveal code-vs-data split. **DONE / COLLAPSED 2026-05-30** ‚Äî surprise finding: **banks 03‚Äì14 are almost entirely DATA.** Stub counts: banks 3-9,11-13 = **0**, bank 10 (audio) = 1, bank 14 = 3. **All ~495 bytecode subs live in banks 0/1/2/15** ‚Äî which are already dumped (and hand-annotated). There is no 12-banks-of-bytecode to dump; the engine's *code* is 4 banks, the other 12 are graphics/maps/text/tables. **This is the big reframe: the epic is mostly already done, it just wasn't named.**
- [x] 3a. **`vm_decompile.py` ported to be spec-agnostic ‚Äî DONE 2026-05-30.** Instead of keying on the old mnemonic strings, dispatch now normalizes the mnemonic from the **opcode byte** (`OPCODE_TO_MNEMONIC`, 256-entry) ‚Äî so it consumes EITHER the old hand-annotated files OR fresh `vm-disasm.py` v2 output, same C from both. Also matched the signed-decimal immediate rendering ($89/$8B/$8D/$8F/$AE) in `vm-disasm.py`. Validated against bank 1: **58/131 subs byte-identical** old-vs-new; the other 73 differ ONLY because the new tool has **correct lengths** (49 subs) or **live labels** (24 subs) ‚Äî the decompile *logic* is identical, and grow reproduces its formula exactly. The prereq for decompile-all is cleared.
- [x] 3b. **decompile-all driver ‚Äî DONE 2026-05-30** (`tools/decompile-all.py`). Runs vm-disasm(v2) ‚Üí vm_decompile over the 4 code banks, captures per-sub C, writes `decompiled/bank_NN.c`. **495 subs, ~11.8k lines.**
- [x] 4. **Persisted `decompiled/bank_{00,01,02,15}.c` ‚Äî DONE 2026-05-30.** Byte-deterministic across runs (the only non-determinism, a temp-path provenance line, is stripped). `decompiled/README.md` documents the artifact + reading caveats. **Still uncommitted ‚Äî offer to commit.**
- [ ] 5. **NOW UNLOCKED: drill down per question against the stored C.** The engine reads like a codebase: `decompiled/bank_01.c` = economy (grow `sub_87F0`, etc.), `bank_02.c` = combat/map, `bank_15.c` = kernel bytecode. ~22% `// TODO:` lines = decompiler's semantically-unhandled opcodes ‚Äî the obvious next quality lever (decode 10-20 opcodes/session ‚Üí richer C; each improvement is a one-line regen). The "data interleaved with code" blocker is solved (`$D5`/`$D9` inline jump tables length-decoded in `vm-disasm.py`).
- **DRIFT NOTE (do NOT silently regenerate the 4 hand-annotated banks):** the committed `disasm/{bank_00,01,02,15}_vm.asm` carry hand corrections, resolved string literals, address labels, and a summary footer ‚Äî more valuable than a fresh dump. They also still drive `vm_decompile.py`. Regenerating them with the v2-mnemonic tool would destroy curation **and** break the decompiler until step 3's port lands. The recovered tool is for *fresh* analysis / re-validation, not for clobbering these. The old files' remaining length bugs ($84/$A0/$AA/‚Ä¶) are documented in `vm-disasm.py`'s header ‚Äî fix them in place during the v2 port if anyone re-derives from those files.

### EPIC: 50-fief map data from ROM (not SRAM) ‚Äî REScOPED 2026-05-29
> Goal unchanged: render all 50 maps without hand-capturing 50 SRAM dumps. But the premise changed.
> **Verified finding ([[project_nobunaga_cell_encoding_vm]], re-confirmed 2026-05-29; refined 2026-05-30):** there is NO static *whole-map* table. Tactical maps are **emitted byte-by-byte by per-fief VM bytecode at battle init** (sub `$8903` reads a metatile byte ‚Üí `memcpy_banked` ‚Üí `$7BFD`). The bank-4 `$A57E` table IS the live **per-cell metatile source** (`$8903` reads it one byte at a time, indexed by computed offset) ‚Äî but `render-atlas.py`'s reading of it as a *directly renderable whole-map* was the dead-end; that renderer stays ‚öÝÔ∏è INVALIDATED. The correct path is to run `$8903`, not to read `$A57E` flat.
> **The unblock:** the 2026-05-21 memory scoped the programmatic path as "multi-day ‚Äî build a partial VM interpreter." **That interpreter now exists** (`nobunaga_vm.py`, the one that cracked math32).
>
> **PROGRESS 2026-05-29 ‚Äî ROM‚ÜíSRAM emit routine LOCATED + partially decoded:**
> - Key finding: the captured `*-combat-init.txt.gz` traces are **render-phase (SRAM‚ÜíPPU), taken AFTER the map was loaded** ‚Äî they contain ZERO staging-buffer writes. That's *why* ROM‚ÜíSRAM was never decoded; no existing artifact holds it. It had to be found in code.
> - The emit routine is **bank-2 VM sub `$885E`** (also `$8942`; confirms the memory's `$894A` lead). It loops 5 rows, computes `dest = $7BFD + ‚Ä¶¬∑88 + offset` (88 = the known col stride), and `host_call $CC54` does the metatile-pattern copy.
> - `vm_decompile.py` of `$885E` shows the **map source is selected by `$6F63` (defending province = which fief's map) + `$6FFE` (mode), via pointers around `$B540`‚Äì`$B547` (bank 2)**. So the per-fief map table is `$B540`-area, province-indexed ‚Äî NOT the disproven bank-4 `$A57E`.
- [ ] 1. Characterize the `$B540`-area table (pointer table? per-fief encoding?) + decode `host_call $CC54` (the metatile copy). This is the remaining ROM‚ÜíSRAM unknown.
- [x] **Syscall layer built + working** (`probe-map-emit.py`, 2026-05-29/30). Intercepts `host_call $F226`, reads the param struct from the VM stack (`$02/$03`=`vm_sp`; `struct[0]`=task id ‚Äî NOT the host_call adj byte, which is the struct-pop size), dispatches by task id. With it the emit path runs **clean, no hang** (the earlier crashes were just unresolved syscalls ‚Äî `wait_for_nmi` spinning, the blit losing sync). Decoded syscalls so far: `$10` memcpy_banked, `$11` rng_next, `$13` wait_for_nmi (stub), **`$14` ppu_blit_from_bank** ($C428: reads tile bytes from SRAM pointer `struct[12]` ‚Üí writes `PPUDATA`). Unknown ids auto-stub + log ‚Üí fill in the ~32 over time. **Promote this layer into `nobunaga_vm` next** (it's reusable core capability).
- [!] **COURSE CORRECTION (2026-05-30): `$885E` is the RENDER driver (SRAM staging ‚Üí PPU), NOT the ROM‚ÜíSRAM populator.** It was found via its `$7BFD` references, but those are *reads* ‚Äî it walks the staging buffer ($7BFD + col*88) and blits each column to PPU via task `$14` (which reads `struct[12]`=`$7D05` staging ptr ‚Üí `PPUDATA`). In the Mino dump the staging buffer was *already* populated (1048 nonzero) before `$885E` ran. So the actual ROM‚ÜíSRAM step is a **different, still-unfound routine.**
- [x] 2'. **POPULATOR = bank-2 sub `$8903` ‚Äî WORKING 2026-05-30.** Battle-init driver `$AFE1` calls `$8903` (populate) at `$AFFC`, then `$8977`‚Üí`$885E` (render) at `$AFFF`. Run `probe-map-emit.py traces/mino-save-ram.dmp 8903`: returns clean (`ok=True, depth=0`), fires only `memcpy_banked` √ó110, and reproduces **880/988 (89%) of the cell-grid region `$7BFD-$7FFF`** (up from 2). Three fixes unlocked it:
  1. **`call_bank ($07)` implemented** (see Open above) ‚Äî was derailing the whole run.
  2. **`memcpy_banked` param offsets were wrong** ‚Äî the real struct is `[task][bank][src][dst][len]` at `sp+0/2/4/6/8` (the args sit *immediately* after the task id). The old code read `src=sp+6/dst=sp+8/len=sp+10`, skipping `src` by one word ‚Üí it read a bogus `len=$EB6D` (60 KB) and scribbled the `$05xx` VM stack (THE cause of the old "$EF76 frame-marker" crash, AND why the populate only ever reproduced 2 bytes). Verified against the AFE1 cell-copy: `bank=4 src=$AA38(=$A57E+off) dst=frame-local len=1` ‚Äî i.e. it reads one metatile byte at a time from the **bank-4 `$A57E` table** (so `$A57E` is live after all, as the per-cell source, not the disproven whole-map renderer).
  3. **6502 `SBC (zp),Y` `$F1` + `(zp,X)` `$E1` were missing** from `cpu6502.py` ‚Äî added.
  - Remaining ~11% of the grid (108 bytes) + the 60 pre-`$7BFD` chrome bytes are written by the **render/decoration phase**, not the populate (they appear only in the full `AFE1` run, which now runs end-to-end with no crash, stopping only on the op budget). No regression: cpu6502 / dispatcher / math32 tests all still pass.
  - **NEXT:** decode the populated `$7BFD` grid to terrain types and confirm the Mino 15-clear/26-forest/12-mountain count (the final ground-truth check); then characterize the render-phase overlay (the other 11%) if a full-fidelity buffer is wanted.
- [~] 3. **ROM‚ÜíMap PROVEN 2026-05-30 ‚Äî inputs pinned, no SRAM capture needed.** `$8903`'s *entire* input set: SRAM `$6F63/$6F64` (province) + `$6D9D/$6D9E` (=17, scenario fief-count / 17-vs-50 selector); ROM `$F70E[province]`‚Üímap_id (bank 15) and `$A57E + map_id√ó55` cell pool (bank 4); **zero RAM inputs; mode `$6FFE` is render-only, not a populate input.** `$F70E[0..16] = [15,9,13,20,21,17,19,23,22,31,26,27,25,30,32,14,24]` (province‚Üímap_id; Mino=8‚Üí22; pool has ‚â•33 maps). **Validated:** a *blank* SRAM seeded with only province=8 + `$6D9D`=17 reproduces the Mino grid **byte-for-byte (1027/1027)** vs the SaveRam-seeded run. None of `$6D9D`/`$F70E`/`$A57E` are in `mesen-labels.toml` yet ‚Äî add them.
  - **TOOL BUILT 2026-05-30: `render-rom-to-map.py <province>`** ‚Äî seeds `$6F63`+`$6D9D` ‚Üí runs `$8903` ‚Üí hands `$7BFD` to `render-from-sram`'s decoder. Verified **byte-identical grid to the captured Mino render**. Has `--scenario 17|50`, `--sram <dump>` (validation mode: read province/scenario from a dump, render from ROM), and warns if a TODO syscall fires. Render step is **Path A** (see Inbox PPU ticket for deferred Path B). Loop 0‚Äì16 ‚Üí full 17-fief atlas from ROM alone (do this once 50-fief is settled, to avoid re-runs).
  - [x] **50-fief CONFIRMED 2026-05-30 (Tanba live test).** Blind ROM render of Tanba (province **29**, `--scenario 50`) ran **clean (`ok=True`, NO new/TODO syscall needed)** and matched the actual captured battle dump (`TanmbaBattle.dmp`) **55/55 decoded cells**. Both blind-assumed inputs verified from the dump: `$6F63`=29, `$6D9D`=50. The earlier risk (50-fief needs a different table / extra syscall) is **retired** ‚Äî the code's internal `$6D9D` branch picks the right ROM table and the same machinery handles it. (Raw byte repro 880/1072 = the usual ~18% render-phase chrome; the 55 map cells are exact.) So ROM‚ÜíMap works for **both** scenarios. `mesen-dump.py` added to fetch battle dumps by convention.
  - [x] **FULL 50-FIEF ATLAS GENERATED 2026-05-30** via `render-rom-atlas.py` ‚Üí `atlas/rom-50/` (50 PNGs + terrain-distribution table). **All 50 clean** (1 castle + 1 town each, no unknown cells, no run-fail, no TODO syscalls). **Atlas-wide cross-validation:** every ROM-rendered map reproduces the matching previously-hand-captured fief's terrain counts EXACTLY (Iga 53-clear, Mino 15/26/12, Echigo 12/13/15+13water, Owari 36+17water, Shinano 7/31/15, Suruga 26/6/6/12+3void, Iseshima 8-void, ‚Ä¶) ‚Äî independent proof the whole atlas is correct, not just the 3 byte-checked fiefs. Confirms 17- & 50-fief share the map pool via `$F70E`. New extremes surfaced: Iwashiro(8)/Kiso(18) = ZERO clear (most rugged), Hitachi(10) = 47 clear (most open), Kii(33) = 11 void (most irregular shape).
  - **The 50-fief map epic is essentially CLOSED.** Remaining optional threads: (a) pixel-exact rendering (the ~18% render-overlay chrome ‚Äî Path B / Inbox PPU ticket); (b) feed the terrain-distribution table into the synthesis chapter / dominance-frontier (Parked); (c) add `$6D9D`/`$F70E`/`$A57E` to `mesen-labels.toml`.

### EPIC: AI turn, TOP-DOWN (the "how does the AI choose" decode ‚Äî like the player command-list chapter)
> Chris's framing (2026-05-30): stop spelunking mid-level subs; find "start of AI turn" and work DOWN through all the logic. The AI reuses the SAME command-driver table ($B9B2) as the player menu, so *issuing* a chosen command is trivial ‚Äî the interesting part is *how commands/targets are chosen*. Skeleton found this session:
> ```
> vm_bootstrap ($A778, bank 0)              ‚Üê post-RESET; BECOMES the main game loop
>  ‚îú‚îÄ daimyo_turn_order ($6F0B)             ‚Üê per-season permutation, re-randomized; READ IN NATIVE CODE (not bytecode!)
>  ‚îú‚îÄ sub_A455 ($A455)                      ‚Üê weakness-mark planner (sets daimyo_weakness_flag $6DD4, health-weighted)
>  ‚îú‚îÄ call_bank(1)  [sub_CBB1 = syscall 7]  ‚Üê bank 1 = TURN PROCESSOR (player input + AI executor)
>  ‚îî‚îÄ call_bank(2)                          ‚Üê bank 2 = combat resolution
> ```
> Why mid-level subs ($B79B issuer, $B89B/$B8A0 per-fief driver) had NO direct callers: they're in bank 1, reached via **call_bank(1)** (cross-bank, indirect) + the **$B9B2 driver table** (CALLPTR). The decompiler can't see those edges; that's why bottom-up stalled.
- [x] **1. Bank-1 turn-processor root FOUND 2026-05-30.** Native `$8000` (bank 1) = `4C 9B B8` = **`JMP $B89B`**. So `call_bank(1)` runs **`sub_B89B`** (body `$B8A0`) ‚Äî the per-fief driver IS the turn root. (Native disasm `disasm/bank_01_labeled.asm` is the tool for these trampolines, not the bytecode decompile.)
- [x] **3. AI executor chain MAPPED 2026-05-30** (did this before 2, the calls revealed it):
> ```
> sub_B89B (turn root)  ‚Äî loops provinces local11=0..fief_count:
>   per province (selected_province_idx):
>     - $6DA1 AI-budget counter ++/-- (read+write each step; the per-turn action budget?)
>     - war_helper_d972(prov) && rng_mod(4)   ‚Üí weakness-war check (daimyo_weakness_flag gate, 25%)
>     - board checks sub_D628 / sub_D982 / sub_D609
>     - switch $6CF7[prov] (per-province STATE 0-5)
>     - CALL $B79B ($B989)  ‚Üê command issuer
>         ‚Üí if rest_turns_remaining[$6D67][daimyo] != 0: consume rest, skip
>         ‚Üí else: loop sub_B6B4() pick cmd-idx ‚Üí command_driver_table[$B9B2][idx] ‚Üí run driver (SAME as player menu)
>             sub_B6B4 ‚Üí sub_D14E (cursor/menu-item engine; reads controller via syscall 6 = read_controller)
> ```
> So the AI issues commands through the EXACT player path ($B6B4‚Üí$B9B2 driver), confirming Chris's "AI uses the same map." `$6CF7` = per-province action-state (0-5); `$6DA1` = an AI counter manipulated every step (budget/aggression ‚Äî pin its exact role next). `$B875`/`$B3AA`/`$B4D5` (maybe-train / AI-send / recruit) are likely $B9B2-table targets reached via the driver dispatch, not separate top-level calls.
- [~] **2. Player-vs-AI fork ‚Äî ANSWERED via Lua trace 2026-05-31 (ai-turn-trace.lua).** A 17-fief Miyoshi(d14) game traced `selected_province_idx` ($6F5F) writes: each turn has **Phase A** = a fast deterministic INDEX-order sweep over a fixed ~11-province set (~7 frames, gap 0-1 = an automated SYSTEM batch, candidate economy/harvest or the weakness planner) then **Phase B** = slow SHUFFLED-order processing (gaps), owners spanning d0-d16 with the **player's province interspersed among AI daimyo** = the per-daimyo TURN LOOP in randomized `daimyo_turn_order`. So **player + AI share ONE unified turn loop; the fork is INTERNAL** (player slot ‚Üí read_controller in sub_D14E; AI slot ‚Üí same code auto-resolves). Gate flag = the `mem_7FE7`-family in sub_D14E (exact bit not yet pinned). **MECHANIC FOUND:** `syscall_read_controller` sets `skip_wallclock` ($0089) while a button is held ‚Üí game-time/RNG PAUSES during player input ‚Äî so the trace's giant frame-gaps (670/1347/2740) are real-time with the clock frozen (menu deliberation + battle animation), NOT AI compute; moderate ~20-30f gaps = AI auto-resolving, clock running. Caveat: $6F5F is overloaded (turn-index AND UI cursor), so the exact fork bit needs sub_D14E static work or a `skip_wallclock` probe.
- [ ] **2b (optional). Pin the exact fork bit** ‚Äî hook `skip_wallclock` ($0089) writes (set = player input active) + log `selected_province_idx`, OR static-decode the `mem_7FE7` branch in sub_D14E.
- [ ] **2-LEGACY. Player-vs-AI fork ‚Äî (superseded by 2 above).** The player and AI share `sub_B89B ‚Üí $B79B ‚Üí sub_B6B4 ‚Üí sub_D14E`; the fork (read controller for player vs auto-select for AI) is inside the **menu/cursor engine** (`sub_D14E`, gated by mode flags `mem_7FE7`/`mem_6F79`/`$7FE1`), which is intricate UI code. **Pin it empirically:** Lua write-callback on `selected_province_idx` ($6F5F) + a flag like `$7FE7`, watch which provinces hit `read_controller` (only the player's should). Cleaner than static-decoding the cursor engine. (Turn-ORDER iteration over `daimyo_turn_order` $6F0B is still native ‚Äî separate.)
- [~] **4. War target-selection chain MAPPED 2026-05-31 ‚Äî and it's OWNERSHIP-based, not strength-based (surprise).** `driver_war ($9850) ‚Üí province_select_helper ($879F) ‚Üí sub_8172 (candidate filter) ‚Üí sub_812F (per-mode dispatch) ‚Üí sub_D9B7 (leaf: `fief_to_daimyo_map[cand] == enemy` ‚Äî OWNERSHIP check)`. Candidates are filtered by **adjacency + enemy-ownership + `$6CF7[fief] != 0xFF`** (per-province state gate); `sub_8172` returns the COUNT of valid candidates. **NO troop-`men` comparison in target selection.** ‚üπ REFRAMES the Mutsu invasion: the AI does NOT cherry-pick weak fiefs ‚Äî it picks among adjacent enemy fiefs, and weak ones fall because they LOSE the battle (combat-outcome, not smart targeting). The user's "low troops" instinct was right about the OUTCOME, wrong about the mechanism. **OPEN:** (a) the AI's pick AMONG multiple valid candidates (random? weakness-flag? first?) ‚Äî not yet located; (b) confirm the combat-strength resolution (bank 2). **TESTABLE:** if combat-outcome, the AI should sometimes attack a STRONGER fief and LOSE; if smart-targeting, it only attacks fiefs it outguns. Lua/play test: do AI attacks ever fail?
>   - **EMPIRICAL (2026-05-31, ai-war-target{2,3,4}.lua, 17-fief Miyoshi=d14):** the AI DOES have a target preference (not random) ‚Äî it attacks WEAK (low-men) adjacent enemies. Of the clean AI-vs-AI committed battles (isolating real commits by `$6F63` staying stable ‚â•30 frames, filtering out player-turn artifacts where `$6F63` idles on the player's fief): **3 of 4 hit the min-men adjacent neighbor** (f8‚Üíf4=94, f16‚Üíf8=90, f15‚Üíf8=38), one did NOT (f7‚Üíf8=218 over weaker f16=48). So **"prefer weak, but NOT strict argmin"** ‚Äî likely a winnability ratio (attacker men vs defender men) or strategic value as the real rule, not absolute minimum. `wk` (weakness-mark) was 0 on essentially all targets (marking is rare, ~4%/turn) so it's NOT the target driver. **CONFIRMED 2026-05-31 (ai-war-target4, 6 turns / 5 clean AI battles + earlier): AI attacks its WEAKEST-MEN adjacent enemy ‚Äî 6 of 8 = exact min ‚Äî and does so EVEN WHEN OUTNUMBERED** (min-men attacks at attacker/defender ratio 0.78, 0.71). So **winnability is REFUTED**: the rule is about the TARGET's weakness, not the attacker's advantage. ‚üπ AI attacks the weakest neighbor and combat resolves on strength separately, which is WHY AI attacks sometimes FAIL. This is the complete answer to "why Oda‚ÜíMino / why my 13-man Mutsu fell" ‚Äî weakest adjacent enemy. The ~1/5 exceptions (chose a higher-men target over an available weaker one) ‚Üí refinement OPEN: (a) the real metric may be army POWER (men√ómorale√óarms), not raw men, or (b) the weaker fief was unattackable (pact/alliance). The candidate FILTER is ownership+adjacency+$6CF7 (driver_war chain); the SCORER = this weakest-men preference (located empirically; static locus still open ‚Äî the AI auto-select branch). **‚ñ∂ Optional NEXT: add morale+arms (army power) to the logger to test the exceptions.**
>   - **METHOD CORRECTION 2026-05-31 (Chris): STOP probe-guessing, READ the C.** v5's men-decrease trigger logged NOTHING across 6 battles ‚Äî premise wrong (the WINNER KEEPS the fief's men/gold/rice, so the defender's men can INCREASE on conquest). Three probe iterations spent guessing a signal. Pivoted to reading the decompiled C (the project's actual method) + LABELING as we go (Layer-2). **CODE-READ FINDING: the AI target-selection chain has NO troop-`men` comparison ‚Äî it's pure ELIGIBILITY filtering:** `driver_war ‚Üí province_select_helper ‚Üí count_eligible_targets ($8172) [+ target_eligible_by_cmd $812F + is_enemy_owned $D9B7 + province_state_is_FF $D999]`; `combat_helper_dd3a` filters then calls `syscall16_sram_wrap` (plumbing). The gate is **`province_ai_state` ($6CF7, per-province 0-5/0xFF)**, NOT men. ‚üπ the empirical "weakest-men" (6/8) was **emergent or probe-noise** (that data had confirmed false positives: player-fief idle + before/after double-fires), NOT explicitly coded. Labeled the read subs ($8172/$812F/$8DE1/$D9B7/$D999/$CBBD/$6CF7) ‚Üí propagated to readable C. **‚ñ∂ REAL NEXT (code-walk, not Lua): what WRITES `province_ai_state` non-zero?** Main setter is `sub_98A3` ($98BF: `$6CF7[fief]=arg3`, on ownership change); enumerate its callers + the state values 0-5 to find whether targetability is conquest/event/men-based. That's the actual "how the AI chooses" answer.
>   - **WALKED TO THE BOTTOM 2026-05-31 (code-read, not probes): there is NO AI target-scorer.** The full war-target chain is `driver_war ‚Üí province_select_prompt ($804C) ‚Üí select_province_by_cursor ($D59D) ‚Üí cursor_nav_loop ($D3ED) ‚Üí sub_D14E (NES button decode, bits 1/2/16/32/64/128 ‚Äî SAME as the player menu)`, gated by eligibility (`is_enemy_owned $D9B7` + `province_ai_state $6CF7 != 0xFF`). It **bottoms out in controller input** ‚Äî the AI selects its target by driving the IDENTICAL menu/cursor machinery the human uses (vindicates "the AI uses the same map" at the deepest level). So "weakest-men" / "Oda‚ÜíMino" is **NOT a coded scorer** ‚Äî it's emergent from eligibility + cursor navigation (+ the earlier probe data had false positives). Labeled the chain ($804C/$D59D/$D3ED/$8172/$812F/$8DE1/$D9B7/$D999/$6CF7) ‚Üí readable C. **‚ñ∂ LAST GAP: `sub_D14E`'s AI branch** ‚Äî when it's the AI's turn, what feeds the "button"/cursor (synthetic input? auto-confirm on first eligible? RNG?). That's the only remaining locus of any actual AI "decision" in target selection.
- **NATIVE-CODE WRINKLE:** turn-order iteration + player/AI branch are native 6502, NOT VM bytecode ‚Äî the bytecode‚ÜíC decompiler is blind to them. This epic may need a native-6502 read of the bank-1 `$8000` entry and/or live Lua tracing, not just `decompiled/`.

## Done ‚Äî recent (newest first; trim to ~15, full history is in chapters + git)
- **VM teardown task "A" ‚Äî table-driven dispatch (family consolidation)** (2026-06-03) ‚Äî collapsed the ~50 mechanical opcode arms in `vm_decompile.py` into 3 data tables + 2 generic blocks (`_BINOP` with signedness-cast field, `_UNARY_A` templates, `_op_hex`/`_op_int` operand helpers). Net ‚àí45 lines; dropped a dead duplicate `div` arm. Genuinely-distinct handlers (host_call/switch/ext_op/frame-access/branches) stay explicit by design. Pure refactor: decompiled C byte-identical, all gates green. Skipped task "B" (0-site opcode `verified=` flags = deferred cross-game spec-completeness, not a blocker). [[feedback_high_quality_code_not_more_code]]
- **VM teardown task "C" ‚Äî positive-arg rendering + real arity** (2026-06-03) ‚Äî `vm_decompile.py` `_slot_name` now names arg5+ (positive odd `fp+N`) and the byte-arg subs the quick opcodes can't reach; `_body_arg_count` counts general-opcode arg reads (word+byte) so 13 subs get correct arity (the 6-arg blit wrappers, `scaled_transfer_da24`, `char_classify`/`is_lower`/‚Ä¶ text engine). Last raw `fp+N` eliminated. Migrated one stranded far-key (`dedup_buf` fp-14‚Üílocal5). All gates green. Teardown's "reads naturally" goal met for args. (ROADMAP Inbox ticket, struck.)
- **DECOMPILER: discarded calls now emitted as statements (+1418 calls recovered)** (2026-06-01, commit `6ddd876`) ‚Äî the VM is a stack machine; `vm_decompile.py` parked each `host_call`/`CALL` result in `regA` and only emitted it if something CONSUMED `regA` before the next write. Side-effecting calls whose result was discarded vanished silently ‚Üí `vm_bootstrap`/`render_boot_title_screens`/victory screen/all boot+UI funcs read as empty loops. Fix: `regA` is now a property that flushes a pending call as `func();` on unconsumed overwrite (+ before unconditional `goto` + at function end), tagged with the call's own address. Recovered +1418 call statements (bank_00 +368 / 01 +661 / 02 +326 / 15 +145). Validated: `effect_grow` byte-IDENTICAL, every added line a call stmt, the 18 changed lines are `goto`‚Üíbraces re-folds that ALSO recovered dropped calls (one fixed a real bug ‚Äî missing `effect_war_a()` before a return in the AI attack path); re-run deterministic. **This was the biggest single readability win since decompile-all ‚Äî the boot/UI layer is now legible in C, no bytecode drop needed.** Surfaced while walking the boot sequence with Chris (the C looked like a bare AI-turn loop because the boot calls were dropped).
- **DAIMYO PORTRAITS LOCATED ‚Äî composite face system, bank 8** (2026-06-01, commit `d38ac80`) ‚Äî portraits are NOT stored whole; they're procedurally composed from base-5 face-code parts. `assign_unique_daimyo_face_code` ($DB97) rolls a unique base-5 word into `daimyo_face_code_table` ($6EB1[daimyo]); `compose_upload_daimyo_portrait` ($8086, bank 2) splits it into feature digits and uploads each feature's variant tiles from **bank 8** (`$A604` head / `$A9C4` eyes / `$ABA4` nose / `$AD84` mouth, 5 variants each, new `[prg.bank8]`) to CHR-RAM ‚Üí a 6√ó6 face. **VISUALLY VERIFIED** via new `tools/render-portrait.py` (faces render as recognizable daimyo) ‚Üí `atlas/portrait-{sheet,faces}.png`. Bank pinned via the `ppu_upload_block` bank arg=8. Also fixed 4 rom-xref cross-bank-pointer false positives (filed under bank 2, data is bank 8). Feeds the visual-atlas chapter. [[project_nobunaga_daimyo_portraits]] **Open polish:** exact part-block‚Üínametable layout (the 6√ó6 tile arrangement) is approximated, not pinned.
- **"SEE THE WHOLE PICTURE" EPIC essentially COMPLETE** (2026-05-30) ‚Äî `tools/decompile-all.py` persists `decompiled/bank_{00,01,02,15}.c`: the entire engine's bytecode (495 subs, ~11.8k lines) as readable C, **byte-deterministic**. The 3-step pipeline that took the whole tooling-discipline arc to enable now runs end-to-end: ROM ‚Üí vm-disasm.py (execution-validated lengths) ‚Üí vm_decompile.py (opcode-keyed dispatch) ‚Üí committed C. Reading the engine is now opening a file. Remaining: commit to git; raise decompiler coverage (22% TODO ‚Üí lower by decoding more opcode semantics). See `decompiled/README.md`.
- **`vm_decompile.py` made spec-agnostic** (2026-05-30) ‚Äî the keystone debt from the vm-disasm recovery. Dispatch now normalizes mnemonics from the **opcode byte** (not the spec-specific name string), so the decompiler reads old OR new (v2) disasm interchangeably. Closed via an opcode‚Üícanonical-name table + matching the signed-decimal immediate rendering in vm-disasm. **Validated by a confusion matrix on bank 1:** decompile output differs old-vs-new **iff** the sub contains a length-fixed opcode (49) or a relabeled address (24); 58 subs byte-identical; 0 false either way; grow's formula reproduces exactly. The decompiler is no longer coupled to the (partially-buggy) old files' naming ‚Äî EPIC step 3b (decompile-all) is unblocked.
- **`vm-disasm.py` RECOVERED + EPIC reframed** (2026-05-30) ‚Äî the bulk VM disassembler that had drifted out of `tools/`. Rebuilt on the **execution-validated** `nobunaga_vm.OPCODE_INFO` (not the deleted old spec), with handler-decoded `$D5`/`$D9` variable-length inline jump tables and recursive-descent reachability termination. Validated by an artifact-independent **exact-tiling** test (the `JSR $E823` stub list must tile each bank): **0 misaligned / 495 subs** on banks 0/1/2/15. Two findings fell out: **(a)** the old `_vm.asm` files had **wrong operand lengths** for ~10 opcodes ($84/$86/$88, $A0-$A3, $AA, $AF, $DE/$DF) ‚Äî proven by emulator `vm_pc`-delta probes + ROM handler reads; the old authors were mid-hand-correction (their own comments say "classifier mis-sized‚Ä¶") and never finished; `OPCODE_INFO` is right. **(b)** **banks 03-14 are ~all DATA** (0 bytecode stubs except bank 10=1, bank 14=3) ‚Üí the whole engine's *code* is just banks 0/1/2/15, already dumped. The external sources (NESDEV t=15931, NovaSquirrel `sea16-reference.c`) are a **different VM revision** (offset opcode map: their `$a0`=deref = our `$B0`) and can't arbitrate this ROM ‚Äî only its own handlers can. See the reframed "See the whole picture" EPIC.
- **Map populator `$8903` cracked** (2026-05-30) ‚Äî `call_bank ($07)` implemented (re-entrant native `$8000` runner with `$F226` interception), a long-standing `memcpy_banked` param-offset bug fixed (struct is `[task][bank][src][dst][len]` at sp+0/2/4/6/8; old code skipped `src`, read a 60 KB length, scribbled the VM stack ‚Äî root cause of the "$EF76" crash and the 2-byte populate), and missing 6502 `SBC ($F1/$E1)` opcodes added. Result: `$8903` runs clean and reproduces **880/988 (89%)** of the Mino cell grid. `$A57E` (bank 4) is the live per-cell metatile source. No regression. See the 50-fief EPIC step 2'.
- **Kernel syscall layer promoted into `nobunaga_vm`** (2026-05-30) ‚Äî intercepts `host_call $F226`, dispatches the 23-entry `$C173` table by task id (read from `vm_sp`; bank-switch emulated by reading the target ROM page directly). **16/23 resolved:** 6 emulated (memcpy_banked, rng, set_sprite, palette_write, palette_swap, audio_load_voice), 10 stubbed (PPU/audio/input/nmi-wait/chr ‚Äî moot headless). No regression (cpu6502/dispatcher tests + math32 still exact). Bytecode no longer hangs on syscalls. See [[project_nobunaga_emulator_tools]].
- **math32 ext-op blocker CRACKED** (2026-05-29) ‚Äî `pct_op`/`math32_3arg`/`math32_2arg` derived + emulator-verified via `probe-math32.py`. The standing magnitude blocker across Dam/AI/combat is gone; the B7 table stayed unopened (helpers were the real interface).
- **Tooling-discipline meta-project COMPLETE** (2026-05-29) ‚Äî registration layer (CONTEXT + 3 registries), `/nobunaga` skill, script consolidation (‚àí11/+2, every merge output-verified), trace gzip (2.9 GB‚Üí250 MB lossless), data-provenance system + `data-index.py auto` (145 legacy dumps contextualized ‚Üí backlog clean). The anti-drift thesis applied to its own toolchain.

## How to use this file
End each session by asking the [[notes/claude-code-skill-engineering]] compounding question, applied to *plans*: did anything move? Promote/park/close items here. An item that's been in **Open** for many sessions with no progress is a signal ‚Äî either it's blocked on one thing (name it) or it's actually Parked (be honest).
